</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Deforestation</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">For the computer science term, see <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_(computer_science)" title="Deforestation (computer science)">Deforestation (computer science)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">"Deforest" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/DeForest_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="DeForest (disambiguation)">DeForest (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolivia-Deforestation-EO.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bolivia-Deforestation-EO.JPG/300px-Bolivia-Deforestation-EO.JPG" width="300" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bolivia-Deforestation-EO.JPG/450px-Bolivia-Deforestation-EO.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Bolivia-Deforestation-EO.JPG/600px-Bolivia-Deforestation-EO.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bolivia-Deforestation-EO.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Satellite photograph of deforestation in progress in eastern <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>. Worldwide, 10 percent of wilderness areas were lost between 1990 and 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><b>Deforestation</b>, <b>clearance</b> or <b>clearing</b> is the removal of a <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forest</a> or stand of trees where the <a href="/wiki/Land_conversion" class="mw-redirect" title="Land conversion">land is thereafter converted</a> to a non-forest use.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Examples of deforestation include conversion of forestland to farms, ranches, or urban use. The most concentrated deforestation occurs in <a href="/wiki/Tropical_rainforest" title="Tropical rainforest">tropical rainforests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> About 30% of Earth's land surface is covered by forests.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Prairie#Mesic" title="Prairie">temperate mesic climates</a>, natural regeneration of forest stands often will not occur in the absence of disturbance, whether natural or anthropogenic.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> Furthermore, biodiversity after regeneration harvest often mimics that found after natural disturbance, including biodiversity loss after naturally occurring rainforest destruction.<sup id="cite_ref-Benton_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benton-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>Deforestation occurs for multiple reasons: trees are cut down to be used for building or sold as fuel, (sometimes in the form of charcoal or timber), while cleared land is used as <a href="/wiki/Pasture" title="Pasture">pasture</a> for livestock and plantation. The removal of trees without sufficient <a href="/wiki/Reforestation" title="Reforestation">reforestation</a> has resulted in damage to <a href="/wiki/Habitat" title="Habitat">habitat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> loss and <a href="/wiki/Arid" title="Arid">aridity</a>. It has adverse impacts on <a href="/wiki/Biosequestration" title="Biosequestration">biosequestration</a> of atmospheric <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>. Deforestation has also been used in <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">war</a> to deprive the enemy of cover for its forces and also vital resources. Modern examples of this were the use of <a href="/wiki/Agent_Orange" title="Agent Orange">Agent Orange</a> by the British military in Malaya during the <a href="/wiki/Malayan_Emergency" title="Malayan Emergency">Malayan Emergency</a> and the United States military in Vietnam during the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a>. As of 2005, net deforestation rates have ceased to increase in countries with a per capita <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> of at least US$4,600.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Deforested regions typically incur significant adverse <a href="/wiki/Soil_erosion" title="Soil erosion">soil erosion</a> and frequently degrade into <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/wasteland" class="extiw" title="wikt:wasteland">wasteland</a>.</p>
<p>Disregard of ascribed value, lax forest management and deficient environmental laws are some of the factors that allow deforestation to occur on a large scale. In many countries, deforestation, both naturally occurring and human-induced, is an ongoing issue. Deforestation causes <a href="/wiki/Extinction" title="Extinction">extinction</a>, changes to climatic conditions, <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>, and displacement of populations as observed by current conditions and in the past through the fossil record.<sup id="cite_ref-Benton_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benton-6">[6]</a></sup> More than half of all plant and land animal species in the world live in tropical forests.<sup id="cite_ref-Rainforest_Facts_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rainforest_Facts-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Between 2000 and 2012, <a href="/wiki/Orders_of_magnitude_(area)#108_to_1014_sqm" title="Orders of magnitude (area)">2.3&#160;million square kilometres (890,000 square miles)</a> of forests around the world were cut down.<sup id="cite_ref-nature1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature1-11">[11]</a></sup> As a result of deforestation, only 6.2&#160;million square kilometres (2.4&#160;million square miles) remain of the original 16&#160;million square kilometres (6&#160;million square miles) of forest that formerly covered the Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-nature1_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nature1-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>
